<div id="review_772858381" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/772858381" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365166675p2/13954899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/772858381?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=fantastical-romance">fantastical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=series-opener">series-opener</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer772858381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12340215732759653368">Decent plot. Likeable characters. Sexy, too. Weak and sometimes frustrating writing style, even though I appreciated the absence of excessive profanity and vulgar terms for female anatomy. So, to be fair, I will elaborate on why this writing is weak, IMO. <br/><br/>Some of the dialogue is just silly, especially given the characters are demons and necromancers. Examples: <br/><br/>"That magic using bastard never had a chance against my little enforcer." (p. 209)<br/><br/>Jacob repeatedly calls Bella "my little enforcer" and "</span>
  <span id="freeText12340215732759653368" style="display:none">Decent plot. Likeable characters. Sexy, too. Weak and sometimes frustrating writing style, even though I appreciated the absence of excessive profanity and vulgar terms for female anatomy. So, to be fair, I will elaborate on why this writing is weak, IMO. <br /><br />Some of the dialogue is just silly, especially given the characters are demons and necromancers. Examples: <br /><br />"That magic using bastard never had a chance against my little enforcer." (p. 209)<br /><br />Jacob repeatedly calls Bella "my little enforcer" and "my little flower" ( ick. Sounds avuncular and patronizing to me). <br /><br />"Holy cow!" (says the killer sorceror. Good golly.) <br /><br />Many sentences are too wordy, long, and poetic. Some dialogue includes academic sounding words where they simply do not fit. The dialogue and the narrative feels like a mix of scholarship and flowery storytelling. Not real.<br /><br />Also, some odd metaphors. Examples:<br /><br />"pain blossoms brutally" (really? It blossoms??)<br /><br />p 359: "the hail of iron that swept towards them was a flock of blades..."<br /> (A "flock" of blades? and a mixed metaphor.)<br /><br />*<b>But my biggest problem is </b> how Frank re-names the characters in consecutive sentences. This de-personalizes the character and confuses me. Below, I show two paragraphs: <br /><blockquote>"The Enforcer looked up at the wind demon blankly. The ground between Elijah's feet split apart. The warrior took to the air in reflex." (p. 327)</blockquote>Is it only me? Doesn't that read as if there are four different characters in the scene?? Oh, but no. Only two, because the author calls Elijah by two other labels here: the wind demon, the warrior. However, the Enforcer (Jacob) is also a kind of warrior, and also a kind of demon, so...I had to pause a moment...and think. This kind of writing interrupts the flow. It is irritating, and it sounds clunky, unnatural. <br /><br />Here is another example of the same kind of confusing re-naming: <blockquote>"Suddenly Legna shivered, her entire body locking up. The empath suddenly went lax, falling back on the floor, blacking out. But then an eerie soft breeze ruffled the unconscious woman's dress and hair. A moment later her eyes opened and she sat back up." (p. 347)</blockquote>So, how many characters here? Yes, I know these sentences are all refering to Legna, but again, I had to pause a moment. Why? Because there are two kidnapped women in that scene. Did something happen to each of them? This writing style impedes the flow of the story, for me. An instant is all it takes. Poof! I am snapped out of the sorceror's pentagram and yanked into syntax study. <br /><br /> Is this really what authors want?? To pull readers from the grip of the drama? I have seen this referencing and re-referencing style in books by other authors. It is not only Frank. Maybe Frank's more recent publications are better.<br /><br />Or...Maybe the problem is me, but this is Kathleen's review, so the writer can write whatever the reviewer wants. (How did that sound? Awful, right?)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12340215732759653368" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97302732" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97302732" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2043222-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577660807p2/2043222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97302732?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/2043222-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97302732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11176213965183782309"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.demonloversbooksandmore.com/2011/11/nightwalkers-series.html'>http://www.demonloversbooksandmore.co...</a><br/><br/>This was a really interesting start to what promises to be an interesting series. <br/><br/>Jacob is the demon king's Enforcer. That means he enforces their laws on any of his people found consorting with humans. Their bestial natures are too much for humans-especially at the Beltane and Samhain moons-May and October. They call it the Hallowed madness. <br/><br/>Enter Isabella.<br/><br/>She falls out of her apartment window and Jacob catches her...mid-air! He is instantly connected to </span>
  <span id="freeText11176213965183782309" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.demonloversbooksandmore.com/2011/11/nightwalkers-series.html">http://www.demonloversbooksandmore.co...</a><br /><br />This was a really interesting start to what promises to be an interesting series. <br /><br />Jacob is the demon king's Enforcer. That means he enforces their laws on any of his people found consorting with humans. Their bestial natures are too much for humans-especially at the Beltane and Samhain moons-May and October. They call it the Hallowed madness. <br /><br />Enter Isabella.<br /><br />She falls out of her apartment window and Jacob catches her...mid-air! He is instantly connected to her, and she suddenly feels choking and burning, and smells smoke. I guess she felt empathy towards the demon Jacob had been hunting-his buddy Saul had been summoned, and once summoned, a demon becomes the slavering bloodthirsty creature we all think of when we hear the word demon. Well, Bella kills Saul, saving her and Jacob's life, but Bella's like 5 foot nothing and human, so wtf? Oh wait, it seems she may not be so human after all-part druid. And while Jacob seems to be breaking the rules he holds so sacred, really he and Bella are imprinting-their souls are recognizing each other. <br /><br />They have to keep Isabella safe, figure out how to save other demons from the necromancers who keep summoning them, and how to tell demonkind that the times they are-a-changing.<br /><br />I liked the idea of the world Jacquelyn Frank created, and I love the demons so far. Bella has some interesting powers, and Jacob is a fantastic hero. All of the supporting characters have me excited for their stories too.<br /><br />I also didn't like how every time Jacob was with Bella the word used to describe him was repeatedly "violent." He actually wasn't violent with her, and the author kept saying how he bruised her and left long red cuts from his claws, but it was not in a just a little too rough way. It was really annoying. Jacob was gentle and protected her, so it seemed out of character. <br /><br />Other than that, the descriptions and the world-building were great and I can't wait to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/702051.Gideon__Nightwalkers___2_" title="Gideon (Nightwalkers, #2) by Jacquelyn Frank" rel="nofollow noopener">Gideon</a> next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11176213965183782309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1080226759" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1080226759" />
    <a title="Ally" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35072420-ally"><img alt="Ally" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491248537p2/35072420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1080226759?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ally" href="/user/show/35072420-ally">Ally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1080226759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17188142578051738360">I don't even know where to start.<br/><br/>This story had so much potential to be good. There was magic, romance, action, sex, humor here and there. So why did it suck?!<br/><br/>First of all, the dialogue was so cheesy it made me cringe. Isabella and Jacob (lol yes, those are their names...) talk to each other like pure words are enough to shatter their fragile bones. They dote on one another - obviously, because then it's not love in a paranormal romance if they don't, is it? - and it's truly hard to stomach afte</span>
  <span id="freeText17188142578051738360" style="display:none">I don't even know where to start.<br /><br />This story had so much potential to be good. There was magic, romance, action, sex, humor here and there. So why did it suck?!<br /><br />First of all, the dialogue was so cheesy it made me cringe. Isabella and Jacob (lol yes, those are their names...) talk to each other like pure words are enough to shatter their fragile bones. They dote on one another - obviously, because then it's not love in a paranormal romance if they don't, is it? - and it's truly hard to stomach after the seventh or eighth time Jacob calls Bella "little flower." Seriously, that's probably the stupidest fucking nickname that I've ever heard. And it's only a testament to how nauseating the relationship is as a whole. This is a couple that I imagine fights over who loves who more behind the scenes; I just thank the good lord above that I didn't have to read that, but the stuff I <i> did </i> have to read bordered on psychotic.<br /><br />And, big shocker, Bella's a virgin. Because romance isn't good unless someone rejects the other one out of innocence and then the experienced one feels rapey, apparently. Jacob is afraid to "go there" with Bella and he even points out that the word "sex" makes her uncomfortable when he says it out loud in front of her (BITCH ARE YOU SERIOUS) and I'm supposed to want to read a sex scene between Tweedle Dee and Tweedle Dumb from this now? In true PNR form, Jacob gets mad at Isabella for arousing him and threatening the control he has over himself and his power a couple times before they're like "lol fuck it" and have sex. Even bigger shocker: They find ways to control themselves and the sex is fine. Written in a horridly confusing, strange, and unengaging way, but we get the sex nonetheless.<br /><br />I really liked the Demons and their affinities with the Earth, and the creativity that went into each Demon's powers and special abilities, even differentiating between sexes. This all was fleshed out pretty well - which bumped this rating up from 1 star to at least 2 - and I have hardly any complaints about that aspect. If anything, I wish there was more of the action dealing with magic. Isabella is a scholar, so most of what makes up the plot is research-based events like studying Demons and figuring things out, blah blah blah. Frankly, I just didn't like Isabella at all so any part with her drove me nuts and I'm probably biased as to how the book should've lent its space to characters and action. Since the main characters annoyed the hell out of me, I would've liked for them to either be written differently or the plot to take root more in the story and action, not develop as a subsequent factor of their romance. Because the romance was stupid.<br /><br />This is probably only something that bothered me, but the author wrote out every single thing in the narration so that the reader is clear on what each sentence means in depth. If you're that fucking stupid that you can't "read between the lines" or grasp more than one meaning from a goddamn sentence, then go back to fourth grade and figure it out. The book literally could've been half its length if every piece of dialogue wasn't followed by an explanation of the emotion conveyed in the quote. Holy Moses, it's common sense. The implications of every. single. action. don't need to be spelled out for the reader. And honestly, nothing in this book is that hard to follow, so it's not like there were confusing parts that necessitated the explanations. Unless, like I said, you're stupid. If I had to read one more time that Isabella felt understandably sad after hearing bad news, AND THEN SEVENTEEN REASONS WERE GIVEN WHY ANYWAY IN EXCRUCIATING DETAIL, I was going to burn the book.<br /><br />Also, what was the ending??? I can't even explain it. I don't even understand the last couple pages. It felt like a preview for a second book, but it wasn't marked at all and ended abruptly. So when you're done with the final page you're like "lol wut where's the rest" but don't get it. I can't even say it was disappointing because I'm not even sure what happened.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And Jesus H. Christ, does every female protagonist have to be pregnant at the end of every book that was ever published in this genre since the beginning of time? Evidently the answer to my recurring question is yes, because lo and behold, Isabella tells Jacob that she's, like, four days pregnant or something. See what unprotected sex gets you, ladies and gentlemen? Demon-Druid hybrid babies. Unplanned ones. I'm not even mad that they're going to have a baby. Unprotected sex isn't the issue here. It's the fact that they've only known each other for, what's it been now, maybe a week? And now they're pregnant? Fuck Destiny, that's bullshit. I don't care that they're destined to be together forever because they're Imprinted (aka soul mates) because we barely even got a real relationship developed, and now we're expected to watch these idiots handle a baby. LOL nope, I'm out. My patience was wearing thin already, and that little nugget of information solidified my loss of interest.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I definitely won't be continuing this series. I'm so emotionally and psychologically unattached to this story, the characters, and the fate of their world that I couldn't start and finish the second book even if I tried. Really really hard. If this book is any indication of how this author writes characters, it doesn't matter how interesting they were at some point in this story - they'll only be brutally massacred in their own story, and that's something I'm definitely not sticking around to witness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17188142578051738360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RCdH+c9ky9zeb9gSniTTh3ydRh/qmRCW2qi1LgJvOAO2K89pZO7gWtk5c8sJ15lSZrPU6Z9bhTKf/Rwd1DEtPw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nPLAwu4o27+ZshV+89lMYJBLGzEKAB6PGszpODWhQ8Ru/khSRaLwOZ7kvqdkKga1imWJx3/CiytfmUAL4/9W+A==')})
  }

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/107202-jacob">Quotes from Jacob</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Whenever I see you, I am overcome with the urge to be rooted within you, to be buried deep so your body can nourish me.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/314753-whenever-i-see-you-i-am-overcome-with-the-urge">25 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Do you think, little flower, that there will ever come a day when you regret meeting me?” he asked quietly.<br />“Yes,” she said simply.<br />“I see,” he said tightly.<br />“Would you like a specific date?”<br />“You are teasing me,” he realized suddenly.<br />“No, I’m dead serious. I have an exact date in mind.”<br />Jacob pulled back to see her eyes, looking utterly perplexed as her pupils sparkled with mischief.<br />“What date is that? And why are you thinking of pink elephants?”<br />“The date is September 8, because, according to Gideon, that’s possibly the day I will go into labor. I say ‘possibly,’ because combining all this human/Druid and Demon DNA ‘may make for a longer period of gestation than usual for a human,’ as the Ancient medic recently quoted. Now, as I understand it, women always regret ever letting a man touch them on that day.”<br />Jacob lurched to his feet, dropping her onto her toes, grabbing her by the arms, and holding her still as he raked a wild, inspecting gaze over her body.<br />“You are pregnant?” he demanded, shaking her a little. “How long have you known? You went into battle with that monster while you are carrying <i>my</i> child?”<br />“<i>Our</i> child,” she corrected indignantly, her fists landing firmly on her hips, “and Gideon only just told me, like, five seconds ago, so I didn’t know I was pregnant when I was fighting that thing!”<br />“But . . . he healed you just a few days ago! Why not tell you then?”<br />“Because I wasn’t pregnant then, Jacob. If you recall, we did make love between then and now.”<br />“Oh . . . oh Bella . . .” he said, his breath rushing from him all of a sudden.<br />He looked as if he needed to sit down and put a paper bag over his head. She reached to steady him as he sat back awkwardly on the altar. He leaned his forearms on his thighs, bending over them as he tried to catch his breath. Bella had the strangest urge to giggle, but she bit her lower lip to repress to impulse.<br />So much for the calm, cool, collected Enforcer who struck terror into the hearts of Demons everywhere.<br />“That is not funny,” he grumbled indignantly.<br />“Yeah? You should see what you look like from over here,” she teased.<br />“If you laugh at me I swear I am going to take you over my knee.”<br />“Promises, promises,” she laughed, hugging him with delight. Finally, Jacob laughed as well, his arm snaking out to circle her waist and draw her back into his lap.<br />“Did you ask . . . I mean, does he know what it is?”<br />“It’s a baby. I told him I didn’t want to know what it is. And don’t you dare find out, because you know the minute you do I’ll know, and if you spoil the surprise I’ll murder you.”<br />“Damn . . . she kills a couple of Demons and suddenly thinks she can order all of us around,” he taunted, pulling her close until he was nuzzling her neck, wondering if it was possible for such an underused heart as his to contain so much happiness.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/826945-do-you-think-little-flower-that-there-will-ever-come">16 likes</a>
            </nobr>
